<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxucGxheWVyX3N0YXRzIDwtIG5mbHJlYWRyOjpsb2FkX3BsYXllcl9zdGF0cyhzZWFzb25zID0gbW9zdF9yZWNlbnRfc2Vhc29uKCksXG4gICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgICAgIHN0YXRfdHlwZSA9IFwib2ZmZW5zZVwiKVxuYGBgIn0= -->

```r
player_stats <- nflreadr::load_player_stats(seasons = most_recent_season(),
                                            stat_type = "offense")
```

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-chunk-end -->


<!-- rnb-text-begin -->


`nflreadr::load_player_stats()`. Arguments include:

* `seasons=`: numeric vector, or use the `most_recent_season()` function
* `stat_type=`: takes "offense", "defense", or "kicking"
*  `file_type=`: takes "rds" (default), "qs", "csv", or "parquet"


From the book:

> As an example, letâ€™s say you need to get Patrick Mahomesâ€™ total passing yard and attempts from the 2022 season. You could do so via load_pbp() but, if you do not need further context (such as down, distance, quarter, etc.), using load_player_stats() is much more efficient.

Below, I'm taking the weekly, box-score level receiving stats, and summarizing them for the pass catchers for the Steelers.


<!-- rnb-text-end -->

<!-- rnb-text-begin -->

  
Some of these statistics won't have any meaning summed (or possibly by taking an average), so I'll dig into each one to get clearer on that.
  
This looks like a good article on [EPA](https://bestballstats.com/expected-points-added-a-full-explanation/#:~:text=Expected%20Points%20Added%20(EPA)%20is,evaluate%20team%20and%20player%20performance.).

<!-- rnb-text-begin -->



### Run success rate 


<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxucGxheV9ieV9wbGF5XzIwMjQgJT4lIFxuICBmaWx0ZXIocGxheV90eXBlID09ICdydW4nLFxuICAgICAgICAgcGxheSA9PSAxLFxuICAgICAgICAgIyBhbiBOQSBydXNoZXIgaW5kaWNhdGVzIGEgcWJfc2NyYW1ibGUsIHNvIEknbGwgZmlsdGVyIHRob3NlIG91dCBvZiB0aGlzXG4gICAgICAgICBxYl9zY3JhbWJsZSAhPSAxLCBcbiAgICAgICAgICFpcy5uYShkb3duKSkgJT4lIFxuICBncm91cF9ieShwb3N0ZWFtLCBydXNoZXIpICU+JSBcbiAgc3VtbWFyaXNlKGNhcnJpZXMgPSBuKCksIFxuICAgICAgICAgICAgc3VjY2Vzc19yYXRlID0gbWVhbihzdWNjZXNzKSxcbiAgICAgICAgICAgIC5ncm91cHMgPSAnZHJvcCcpICU+JSBcbiAgZmlsdGVyKGNhcnJpZXMgPj0gMjApICU+JSBcbiAgYXJyYW5nZSgtc3VjY2Vzc19yYXRlKSAlPiUgXG4gIG11dGF0ZShyYW5rX3N1Y2Nlc3NfcmF0ZSA9IHJhbmsoLXN1Y2Nlc3NfcmF0ZSkpXG5gYGAifQ== -->

```r
play_by_play_2024 %>% 
  filter(play_type == 'run',
         play == 1,
         # an NA rusher indicates a qb_scramble, so I'll filter those out of this
         qb_scramble != 1, 
         !is.na(down)) %>% 
  group_by(posteam, rusher) %>% 
  summarise(carries = n(), 
            success_rate = mean(success),
            .groups = 'drop') %>% 
  filter(carries >= 20) %>% 
  arrange(-success_rate) %>% 
  mutate(rank_success_rate = rank(-success_rate))
```

<!-- rnb-source-end -->

<!-- rnb-chunk-end -->


<!-- rnb-text-begin -->


I'm curious about the success rate of Fields' runs, whether they were designed or a scramble. It doesn't look like the `qb_scramble` field is coded with any scrambles to date, so I'll let that one simmer for a few weeks.


<!-- rnb-text-end -->


<!-- rnb-chunk-begin -->


<!-- rnb-source-begin eyJkYXRhIjoiYGBgclxucGxheV9ieV9wbGF5XzIwMjQgJT4lIFxuICAjIG1hcmtpbmcgcGxheV90eXBlID0gJ3J1bicgcmVtb3ZlcyBRQiBrbmVlbHMgXG4gIGZpbHRlcihwbGF5X3R5cGUgPT0gJ3J1bicsXG4gICAgICAgICBydXNoZXIgPT0gJ0ouRmllbGRzJylcblxuYGBgIn0= -->

```r
play_by_play_2024 %>% 
  # marking play_type = 'run' removes QB kneels 
  filter(play_type == 'run',
         rusher == 'J.Fields')

```
